From kcramakrishna at yahoo.com  Wed Jun  3 13:26:24 2009
From: kcramakrishna at yahoo.com (K.C. Ramakrishna)
Date: Wed Jun  3 13:27:08 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] Safer domain search
Message-ID: <925234.77927.qm@web33101.mail.mud.yahoo.com>


Hi all,

I have been searching for a domain name for a new service we were planning to launch. I shortlisted a few good ones which were available and went back to register them the next week. To my surprise, I found them not available. These are not common names - they are very specific to a niche service and I doubted that somebody else would have thought the of same names at the exact same time.

On googling, I found that Network solutions and some other registrars do something called 'front-running' where they basically block all domain names that were searched for and force you to pay more.

There is a work around to this - Use
http://instantdomainsearch.com/
http://www.saferwhois.com/

Hope this helps somebody.

Thanks,
kc
K. C. Ramakrishna



      
From rajasuperman at gmail.com  Wed Jun  3 15:55:20 2009
From: rajasuperman at gmail.com (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Wed Jun  3 15:56:19 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] Safer domain search
In-Reply-To: <925234.77927.qm@web33101.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
References: <925234.77927.qm@web33101.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <92f9a9560906030325y51dc53b2q131f92d8645c57b7@mail.gmail.com>

On Wed, Jun 3, 2009 at 1:26 PM, K.C. Ramakrishna
<kcramakrishna@yahoo.com> wrote:>
> On googling, I found that Network solutions and some other
> registrars do something called 'front-running' where they
> basically block all domain names that were searched for and
> force you to pay more.

After a couple of days, the domains typically become available
again.  icann.org permits some registrars to register a domain
for 2 days without making any payment.  And if payment is not
made, the registration expires.  This loop hole is exploited by
evil registrars.

I learnt this the hard way as well and was equally shocked.

Best way to check domain name availability is to query your
own dns server or look up the whois database.

- Raja

The following seems to be worth following up on.

 http://wave.google.com/

This is a combination of a protocol spec, a reference implementation
and an alpha stage client and server. (Apparently all FOSS).

I don't know too much at this point except that it integrates e-mail,
IRC/chat, collaborative editing (sobby), wikis and blogging. This
already covers a good deal of what I do!

I need to read (so much :-( ) more before saying anything else.

Hello,

On Thu, 04 Jun 2009, Karanbir Singh wrote:
> On 06/03/2009 09:38 PM, pavithran wrote:
>> When I meant RPM is passe I was implying it from the fact tthat ubuntu has
>> eaten over the share of both fedora and opensuse(for a diff reason ) .
>> Fedora started it's spin projects and even started giving the project a new
>> look only after it realised the stiff competition from Ubuntu .
>
> I dont believe that at all, where did you get these stats from ? It just  
> sounds like FUD that someone is pushing your way and people with  
> blinkers on passing it on cause it makes them feel quite hip.

I am sure that the success of Ubuntu has motivated the Fedora
developers to change a few things --- why not!?

Conversely, one could argue that the success of Fedora's timely
release cycles (OK, this is perhaps a bad time to be saying that :-) ) is
probably what led to a few Debian developers and others to create
Ubuntu!

Deistributions can and do learn from each other all the time. At this
point in time, when the number of users is still growing, the
competition is generally a good thing for all distros --- no one is
really _losing_.

Regards,

Kapil.

Windows doesn't even have a integrate package manager!

I would like to know your sources for estimating "market share". Fedora
has consistently grown every release

http://fedoraproject.org/wiki/Statistics

Even assuming that one distribution takes away "market share" of another
distribution, how does that help Linux on the whole? If a distribution
really wants to make a difference, it's goal cannot really be fighting
over the already minuscule share of users instead of concentrating on
the bigger pie.

> Fedora started it's spin projects and even started giving the project a new
> look only after it realised the stiff competition from Ubuntu .

Err, you obviously have your history wrong. Fedora spins evolved from
the merger of core and extras repository which has nothing to do with
any other distribution. You seem to think distributions are continuously
in competition while in reality, much of the software in a distribution
is from common upstream sources and Fedora is very active there

http://fedoraproject.org/wiki/Red_Hat_contributions

> are still running windows

The vendors and analysts have published such information. There is zero
dispute about this. Windows continues to remain the majority by far on
netbooks, laptops and desktops but hey if your analysis is just between
friends, then of course I can claim 100% Linux even.

From stylesen at gmail.com  Thu Jun  4 13:13:57 2009
From: stylesen at gmail.com (Senthil Kumaran S)
Date: Thu Jun  4 13:14:38 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Authentication problem in SVN
In-Reply-To: <fde97d960906032247v64e63b80h9aeb46ff0cf9b83a@mail.gmail.com>
References: <fde97d960906032247v64e63b80h9aeb46ff0cf9b83a@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <5ef2113c0906040043q230c21d4qe0d0abb58ee1fe80@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

On Thu, Jun 4, 2009 at 11:17 AM, mettur salem <metturmohan2009@gmail.com> wrote:
> ?under the folder of conf
>
> -rw-r--r-- 1 apache apache? 755 2009-06-03 21:41 authz
> -rw-r--r-- 1 apache apache?? 46 2009-04-29 20:01 passwd
> -rw-r--r-- 1 apache apache 1449 2009-06-03 21:41 svnserve.conf
>
> if i give the some restriction in svnserve.conf??? file this is not able to
> apply while access? via http of svn pages in local lan ??? authz file is not
> responses? any upgradation required? ( related to Modules loaded? in http
> file )

svnserve.conf has to do nothing with access over http://, it is for
svn:// access and svnserve daemon. So whatever you do inside conf
directory of a repository it wont have any effect for http:// access.
This is mentioned in those files clearly in the comments. Please read
http://svnbook.red-bean.com/, in order to understand the various
access methods of subversion which is clearly explained.

> ie http://192.168.1.2/repos/svn??? --- it allows all to access and commit
> and checkout? for all the repositary? i apply? restriction? as per senthil
> says? but it is not effect

This may be due to many reasons. One such reason is, you don't have
the required authentication modules loaded in apache, like mod_auth,
mod_authz, mod_authz_svn, etc.

The following command will help you to identify this:

`sudo which httpd` -l

> 1.http authenticaion file is kept in? /etc/svn-auth?? ie user password are
> stored here
> 2. subversion configuration file is kept in? /etc/
> httpd/conf.d/subversion.conf
>
>
> subversion.conf
>
> <Location /repos>
> ??? DAV svn
> ?? SVNParentPath? /repos
> ?? AuthType Basic
> ? AuthName "Snowserver1 Subversion Repositories"
> ????? AuthUserFile /etc/svn-auth-file

As per 1. your file is " /etc/svn-auth" but you have put
"/etc/svn-auth-file" in your apache configuration.

> ?? <LimitExcept GET PROPFIND OPTIONS REPORT>
> ????? Require valid-user
> ?? </LimitExcept>
> </Location>

Do not put "Require valid-user" inside <LimitExcept> section, just put
this after "AuthUserFile" directive.

Having said that, I would like you to go through
http://svnbook.red-bean.com/ which has all the information regarding
subversion administration.

Thank You.
-- 
Senthil Kumaran S
http://www.stylesen.org/

Subject: [Ilugc] [Cross-Posted] [Commercial] Quality Assurance Engineer
 openings at Red Hat, Pune
Message-ID: <4A28AF2A.3060801@gmail.com>

The following Quality Assurance Engineer roles are in the process of 
being hired at Red Hat (Pune). Interested candidates may send in their 
resumes to careers-in at redhat dot com. Please mention the role in the 
subject line of the mail.

*Quality Assurance Engineer*

As a Quality Assurance Engineer you are expected to set the quality 
standards for a small product or, for a significant area of large 
product. You are expected to develop test cases and test plans for areas 
of ownership and, would be capable of directing the efforts of 3 to 4 
quality engineers. You should be able to effectively and accurately 
communicate testing status to management and other interested parties. 
You should be able to interface with customer and partner quality 
organizations and, can be relied on to exercise good judgment around 
critical issues. You should be able to work with developers to resolve 
issues and analyze data in a timely manner. You are expected to process 
in-depth understanding of the testing processes and standards. Primary 
focus is on API, WebUI, and client tool testing.

Job Requirements:

Test Automation and Development Job Requirements:

     * Knowledge of how to use a defect tracking system (JIRA or 
Bugzilla preferred).
     * Knowledge of how to use a revision control system (Git, 
Subversion,or CVS preferred).
     * Good skills in at least three of: Java, Python, Perl, BASH, or Ruby.
     * Previous experience with automated testing tools.
     * Expertise in Selenium and/or JUnit a major plus.
     * Demonstrated skills in Linux systems administration.
     * Basic knowledge of database usage and ability to write SQL.

*JBoss Operations Network Quality Assurance Engineer*

JON Essential Duties and Responsibilities: As a Quality Assurance 
Engineer for JBoss Operations Network, you will be responsible for 
expanding our existing test automation framework, as well as evaluating 
and implementing new Open Source tools to verify the quality of the 
product. The job will have you working with an international team of 
Software Developers and fellow QA Engineers. Primary focus is on WebUI 
automation and agent testing. Will be responsible for writing test plans 
and test cases for assigned functional areas. Will then be responsible 
for running manual tests, writing automated tests, and running automated 
tests. Also responsible for writing, verifying, and closing bugs on each 
version of the product.

JON Job Requirements:

     * Knowledge of how to use a defect tracking system (JIRA or 
Bugzilla preferred).
     * Knowledge of how to use a revision control system (Subversion 
preferred).
     * Ability to read and write Java code.
     * Previous experience with automated testing tools.
     * Expertise in Selenium a major plus.
     * Demonstrated skills in Middleware and/or application servers.
     * Basic knowledge of database usage and ability to write SQL.

*Satellite and Proxy Quality Assurance Engineer*

Satellite/Proxy Essential Duties and Responsibilities: As a Quality 
Assurance Engineer for the Red Hat Network Satellite and Proxy products, 
you will be responsible for expanding our existing test automation 
frameworks, as well as evaluating and implementing new Open Source tools 
to verify the quality of the product. The job will have you working with 
an international team of Software Developers and fellow QA Engineers. 
Primary focus is on API, WebUI, and client tool testing. Will be 
responsible for writing test plans and test cases for assigned 
functional areas. Will then be responsible for running manual tests, 
writing automated tests, and running automated tests. Also responsible 
for writing, verifying, and closing bugs on each version of the product.

Satellite/Proxy Job Requirements:

     * Knowledge of how to use a defect tracking system (Bugzilla 
preferred).
     * Knowledge of how to use a revision control system (Git, 
Subversion,or CVS preferred).
     * Good skills in at least two of: Java, Python, Perl, BASH, or Ruby.
     * Previous experience with automated testing tools.
     * Expertise in Selenium and/or JUnit a major plus.
     * Excellent skills in reading and writing technical documentation 
in English.
     * Demonstrated skills in Linux systems administration.
     * Basic knowledge of database usage and ability to write SQL.
     * Basic previous experience in Solaris administration a plus.

*Test Automation and Development Quality Assurance Engineer*

Test Automation and Development Essential Duties and Responsibilities: 
As a Quality Assurance Engineer for Test Automation and Development, you 
will be responsible for creating, writing, and maintaining Selenium 
automated tests, test frameworks in Java, and XML-RPC JUnit automated 
tests. You will need to be able to work with other teams in implementing 
integration and maintenance of Hudson continuous integration 
environment. Must have a willingness to be involved in manual testing as 
needed (but minimal). Will be responsible for writing test plans for 
feature areas and then writing, executing, and automating test cases.

Test Automation and Development Job Requirements:

     * Knowledge of how to use a defect tracking system (JIRA or 
Bugzilla preferred).
     * Knowledge of how to use a revision control system (Git, 
Subversion,or CVS preferred).
     * Good skills in at least three of: Java, Python, Perl, BASH, or Ruby.
     * Previous experience with automated testing tools.
     * Expertise in Selenium and/or JUnit a major plus.
     * Demonstrated skills in Linux systems administration.
     * Demonstrated skills in Middleware and/or application servers.
     * Basic knowledge of database usage and ability to write SQL.

ILUGC Monthly Meet (Jun 13th):-
==============================

Time : Sat Jun 13th 15:00 IST 2009
Venue: ADI-TeNeT Seminar Hall,
       Room No: CSD 320,
       Electrical Science Block (ESB),
       IIT-Madras.

> Talk 1: Emacs-Org-Mode
Speaker : Ashok Gautham
Duration: ~40mins

Org-Mode is an emacs major mode that can be used for keeping notes,
maintaining ToDo lists, doing project planning, and authoring with
a fast and effective plain-text system. It comes in with a powerful 
set of functions for maintaining spreadsheets and agendas.

Link: http://orgmode.org/

> Talk 2: Linux Config Files Series I - CUPS
Speaker : Raman P
Duration: ~40mins

This series of talk will cover most of the standard configuration
files in Linux based system. In this talk, Speaker will cover the
configuration files of the Common UNIX Printing System (CUPS), 
a standards-based open source printing system.

Link: http://www.cups.org/

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Fri Jun  5 12:58:04 2009
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Fri Jun  5 13:04:14 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] Disks/controller/interfaces
In-Reply-To: <b89799040906042350v1c9dd362rfa6bdc86b566da65@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0906051243400.1107-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

On 12:20pm, Ashish Verma wrote:

> 1. SCSI / IDE / SATA / Firewire / UHCI - Are these types of 1)
> cables, 2) disks, 3) interface on the disk, 4) connectors on the
> mother board (like PCI) or 5) standards / protocols 

Standards. But it is a combination of all the above (1-5)

> 2. Controller - is it something on a peripheral or on the
> motherboard.

I hope, you are referring SCSI Controller cards. Today in Low-end
mother boards, IDE and SATA controllers are in-built. In high-end
mother boards, SCSI may-be in-built. If it is not in-built in the 
MB, you use PCI controller card to interface with SCSI HDD.

Bye :)
-- 
Bharathi S

From kapil at imsc.res.in  Fri Jun  5 20:57:02 2009
From: kapil at imsc.res.in (Kapil Hari Paranjape)
Date: Fri Jun  5 20:57:51 2009
Subject: Netbook OS's (Was Re: Moblin (Was Re: [Ilugc] The path forward for
	Linux is child's play))
In-Reply-To: <20090604174713.GC16235@imsc.res.in>
References: <f3d38c890906040759j5b269948od201122abdbc535b@mail.gmail.com>
	<20090604174713.GC16235@imsc.res.in>
Message-ID: <20090605152702.GA32055@imsc.res.in>

Hello,

 "GNU/Linux on netbooks is dead. Long live GNU/Linux on netbooks!"

:)

Things are exciting in the world of O/S's which are geared towards
netbooks and other light handheld communications devices.

Two that I _have_ tried and both work very nicely with the Acer
Aspire One. (Of course, I continue to use Debian!)

1. www.moblin.org has a moblin v2 for test via a live USB boot or
qemu image.

 Its interface is based on the Sugar interface for the OLPC. Worth
 trying if only for the novelty. Perhaps it will change the way you
 think of the UI.

 You can also try it with qemu/kvm to expand your virtualisation
 horizons :-)

2. Ubuntu has Ubuntu Netbook Remix for Jaunty available as a live USB
boot image. wiki.ubuntu.com/UNR

 This also has an interesting interface based on dual vertical panels
 instead of the usual horizontal ones. It has maximus which can
 maximise screen space for specific applications.

Some that I have not tried:

1. Ubuntu has its UMPC version for Intrepid and Jaunty as a live USB
boot image. This is for low power machines with touchscreens.

2. Android from Google. This needs a download and compile for now. No
bootable image seems to be available.

Also of interest is Maemo.org which has the interface designed by
Nokia for its touchscreen phones.

Ubuntu also plans to release a remix based on the Moblin interface.

Regards,

Kapil.
--

Dear All,

Fibonacci is the annual International Open Source magazine of the Students? Forum for Free/Open Source Software running under Indian Institute of Information Technology and Management Gwalior. This is being released in association with SUN Microsystems and National Resource Center FOSS.

The use of FOSS and FOSS based products deserve a special mention when it comes to academia. FOSS stands as a promising movement for the up gradation of education standards and knowledge sharing worldwide. In this first edition of Fibonacci we salute the pioneering work done or being done in the use of FOSS and FOSS based products in academia.

If you use or know the use of any such software, portal or practice being used or being developed for use in educating people and spreading knowledge, especially at the student level, please let us know so that we may tell the world.  

You may use the form at http://sf-foss.iiitm.ac.in/fibonacci/submitFSI.php (preferred) or alternatively you can mail us the details.

The submission of regular articles is open and may be submitted at the magazine site. The last date of submission of articles is 15th June, 2009.

Hello,

On Sat, 06 Jun 2009, Shrinivasan T wrote:
> > is it just me or are the slides duplicated at each step?
> 
> Okular shows the presentation perfectly.

I think there is some confusion about PDF presentation overlays.
These are usually implemented as duplicated pages with some
additional material.

If you view a PDF presentation in a viewer which just shows you
page-by-page you will see many pages duplicated.

On the other hand running in "presentation mode" in xpdf or evince
or impressive will show you the presentation as the author originally
intended.

Regards,

Kapil.
--

> > Could you please try the following presentation, and let me know if it
> > is useful?
> > http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/glv/presentations/di-git-ally-managing-lov
> >e-letters.pdf
 
> is it just me or are the slides duplicated at each step?

They'll be _almost_ duplicated. It's Beamer's way of trying to produce
animation-type effects. eg. if you want 3 lines of text to appear one
after the other, beamer will create 3 slides where successive slides
have one more line. Viewing it in presentation mode, or simply making
sure that your viewer is set to "fit-page" zoom level should do it.

Subject: NOT SOLVED : [Ilugc] stream.h and fstream.h NOT FOUND problem
In-Reply-To: <28ac23fb0906070134r327a0663xd03d3e6f689d613e@mail.gmail.com>
References: <28ac23fb0906070134r327a0663xd03d3e6f689d613e@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <4A2BA6DC.2030204@lonetwin.net>

Hi Bala,

bala chandar wrote:
> I installed build-essential already.But again it shows the same
> errors.I need to know which library i need to install to get those
> headers.

Firstly, stream.h and fstream.h are not *standard c++ headers*, so they don't 
exist (afaik) in gnu c++ devel. environment. Please use iostream and fstream 
instead[1] ...

#include <iostream>
#include <fstream>

Secondly, you'll probably need the appropriate ubuntu packages corresponding to 
fedora's libstdc++ and libstdc++-devel. I'm sorry, i can't be sure what they are 
since i use fedora, however, they most likely have the same names.

hth,
- steve

[1] http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C%2B%2B_standard_library#Streams_and_Input.2FOutput
[2] http://www.cplusplus.com/doc/tutorial/files/
--

From kapil at imsc.res.in  Mon Jun  8 09:11:42 2009
From: kapil at imsc.res.in (Kapil Hari Paranjape)
Date: Mon Jun  8 09:12:21 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] How to Create My own customized ubuntu iso
In-Reply-To: <28ac23fb0906071931q7607187fhfbb63949b910ab9b@mail.gmail.com>
References: <28ac23fb0906071931q7607187fhfbb63949b910ab9b@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20090608034140.GA30295@imsc.res.in>

Hello,

On Sun, 07 Jun 2009, bala chandar wrote:
> I want to fully customize ubuntu.Boot screen,log in screen,splash
> screen,adding/removing softwares everything to my flavour.

Step 1. Create a customisation that you like on your own desktop (or
if you know how, then do it in a virtual machine). There are standard
configuration programs in the "Preferences" and "Administration"
menus to do this. Take detailed notes.

> I already read about UCK.

Step 2. Create a custom CD. You will need the detailed notes you made
above. This is for people who want to create a Custom Live CD _after_
they are already through with Step 1. The instructions are on the
Ubuntu wiki.

> But i want an easy to follow tutorial regarding all.I hope such one
> is there in the net.

Step 3. Be prepared to maintain your customised Ubuntu. There is no
point in creating a distribution without the support.

I would personally stop with Step 1 and leave 2 and 3 to others.

Kapil.

P. S. Step 0. Use your system for some work. This will give you some
idea about what customisations are needed for your work.
--

Tally is an accounts and inventory management software which is having many  
other features too.

1. do all basic accounting functions,
2. Manage your store and items,
3. do the job costing,
4. manage payroll,
5. get many mis reports which are useful for day today functions,
6. file your tax returns like prepare balance sheet, profit and loss  
statement, VAT forms, TDS, returns, Service tax returns, e-TDS filing,  
Excise forms, FBT reports and forms,
7. maintain budgets, scenarios,
8. calculate interest on pending amount
9. manage data over different locations and synchronize it and many more  
other features.

Is there a open source software available with respect to tally.

openerp (formerly known as tinyerp) has complete accounting and erp also. 
There are many people in India working on customising it for India and it is 
in use in many places in India. Gnukhata is a local initiative, but is not 
fully usable at present. AVSAP is purely financial accounting - does not have 
the complete features you want. If you want something ready to go, openerp is 
your best bet. You could also get some consultant to customise it for you - or 
you could do it your self.

On Mon, Jun 8, 2009 at 12:45 PM, Kannan <kannan4k@gmail.com> wrote:

>
> i have installed the ubuntu 8.10 version.i got the new ubuntu 9.04 cd from
> cananical.
> how can i upgrade the system using this new cd?

Dear Kannan,

You can upgrade Ubuntu to the latest version either with the Alternate
Installation CD, the DVD or an online upgrade. You cannot upgrade to the
latest version using the Live CD sent by Canonical. Do a clean install with
the CD that you have recieved, or download and burn a copy of the Alternate
CD from the website.
From mohan43u at gmail.com  Mon Jun  8 13:15:40 2009
From: mohan43u at gmail.com (Mohan R)
Date: Mon Jun  8 13:16:46 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: stream.h and fstream.h NOT FOUND problem
In-Reply-To: <28ac23fb0906062112s7ff02aedkd9d5ef1c6be425dd@mail.gmail.com>
References: <28ac23fb0906062112s7ff02aedkd9d5ef1c6be425dd@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <h0ifj5$7ir$1@ger.gmane.org>

bala chandar wrote:
> Hai,
> I recently installed Ubuntu 8.10.Actually I need g++ for my project.So
> I installed it through synaptic.I installed g++,g++ 4.1,g++4.2,g++ 4.3
> all shown in synaptic.
> But when i compile my project it says,
> stream.h - No Such File or Directory Found
> fstream.h - No Such File or Directory Found

I think you need to set proper 'CFLAGS' using 'pkg-config'. When I
searched for 'stream.h' it is inside 'directfb' directory.

$ find /usr -name 'stream.h'
/usr/include/directfb/direct/stream.h
$

Then I searched inside '.pc' files, These are the packages which
includes 'directfb' directory.

$ find /usr -name '*.pc' -exec grep -H 'Cflags:.*directfb' {} \;
/usr/lib/pkgconfig/direct.pc:Cflags: -D_REENTRANT
-I${prefix}/include/directfb

/usr/lib/pkgconfig/fusion.pc:Cflags: -I${prefix}/include/directfb

/usr/lib/pkgconfig/directfb.pc:Cflags: -D_REENTRANT
-I${prefix}/include/directfb

/usr/lib/pkgconfig/directfb-internal.pc:Cflags: -D_GNU_SOURCE
-I${prefix}/include/directfb-internal
$

I don't know what kind of programming you are doing, But you need to
include 'directfb' during compilation. Anyone of the below example will
include 'stream.h'

Eg:

$ g++ `pkg-config --cflags --libs 'direct'` -o output somefile.cpp
$ g++ `pkg-config --cflags --libs 'fusion'` -o output somefile.cpp
$ g++ `pkg-config --cflags --libs 'directfb'` -o output somefile.cpp
$ g++ `pkg-config --cflags --libs 'directfb-internal'` -o output
somefile.cpp

For fstream.h, I searched in my system, not able to find, The above
procedure will help you to get 'fstream.h' file's pkg-config.

Regards,
Mohan R.

On Sun, Jun 7, 2009 at 9:42 AM, bala chandar<balachandarlinks@gmail.com> wrote:
> Hai,
> I recently installed Ubuntu 8.10.Actually I need g++ for my project.So
> I installed it through synaptic.I installed g++,g++ 4.1,g++4.2,g++ 4.3
> all shown in synaptic.
> But when i compile my project it says,
> stream.h - No Such File or Directory Found
> fstream.h - No Such File or Directory Found
>
> I m really in need of these headers.Pls help me to get rid of it
> soon.Thank you....
> cheers.....

In the more modern C++ systems, you don't include fstream.h or
iostream.h; the correct form is:

#include <fstream>

using namespace std;

I think gcc and friends will yell at you if you don't follow this.

Regards,
Shash

From freedomyug at gmail.com  Mon Jun  8 19:14:25 2009
From: freedomyug at gmail.com (Gourav Shah)
Date: Mon Jun  8 19:15:07 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] regular expression the check if a string is absent
In-Reply-To: <200906081656.11679.lawgon@thenilgiris.com>
References: <200906081656.11679.lawgon@thenilgiris.com>
Message-ID: <60d395660906080644n437e086cyff0d3fc71565d982@mail.gmail.com>

> I am trying to build a regular expression that will find all strings that
> do
> not start with '2009/'. Any clues?
>

I am assuming you could use grep here, if not, please specify how you intend
to do the pattern matching.

grep has a option to invert match, here is a snip from manpage,
...

       -v, --invert-match
              Invert the sense of matching, to select non-matching lines.
(-v is specified by POSIX.)

so if its grep, you could use,  grep "^2009/"  <FILENAME>

e.g.

$ cat >> /tmp/t.txt
snfgd
fdnbfognbof errgirnbinr
kjfnfbjgnb 434fgv 54y 5obn
2009/ rgerigbir nr
vrgnbn
2009/ y fdgovrf23 3gp 4
bgfbog
232234
565
2009
regtrgm ^[[A^[[A
2009 enfvfrnv evirvir
vornbtr

$ grep "^2009/" /tmp/t.txt
2009/ rgerigbir nr
2009/ y fdgovrf23 3gp 4


$ grep -v "^2009/" /tmp/t.txt
snfgd
fdnbfognbof errgirnbinr
kjfnfbjgnb 434fgv 54y 5obn
vrgnbn
bgfbog
232234
565
2009 enfvfrnv evirvir
vornbtr


Thanks
Gourav

On Tue, 2009-06-09 at 10:57 +0530, Ramkumar wrote:
> Hi Friends,
>                  i would like to delete only Boot Loader in my machine. how
> can i do it. i have dual boot (Linux & Windows XP) machine.
> 

What does this mean? You want to boot into Windows only directly?

Boot your Windows XP CD-ROM, and when it says "Welcome to Setup", hit
the R key to access the recovery console. There is a full description of
the steps needed to do this here:
<http://support.microsoft.com/kb/307654>

At the recovery console, type the following:

	fixmbr

For a full description of the command, see:
<http://www.microsoft.com/resources/documentation/windows/xp/all/proddocs/en-us/bootcons_fixmbr.mspx?mfr=true> and for warnings on the use of the command and more helpful documentation, scroll down to the FIXMBR section on the following page: <http://support.microsoft.com/kb/314058>.
-- 
Regards,
Roshan George <roshan@arjie.com>

From balaviswanathv at gmail.com  Tue Jun  9 14:10:41 2009

Subject: [Ilugc] squid
In-Reply-To: <9cf4b91c0906082228x55c84869w3ee0ae6b2dff7a86@mail.gmail.com>
References: <9cf4b91c0906082228x55c84869w3ee0ae6b2dff7a86@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <3f7e84ea0906090140m144c3567w5b560015c44e5f90@mail.gmail.com>

Hi Rajeshkumar,

Please use acl for this

Syntax:
In Acl listing:

acl block url_regex -i "/etc/squid/squid-block.acl"

In Http_access

http_access allow all
http_access deny block

make sure you have the entries in squid-block.acl file

reload squid and it must work

Regards

Bala

Squid itself offers basic access control and content filtering.

But if you want advanced features (which you will no doubt require
in future), install squidguard.  It works a treat, and is pretty well
documented.

Dear  All,

*Comet* (programming) <http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comet_%28programming%29>,
is reverse Ajax call,  we make a server to push an asynchronous response to
the client with an request, Most of the online streaming server work this
way, even sites like meebo.com, gtalk intergration with gmail are some of
the typical example of the server push technology(Comet). I am trying to
implement the same in on of the application but I got struck, If some of you
had already done this or something similar to this, please do share your
ideas
Some of my attempts

   1. I had tried couple of things with prototype and hidden iframe,
   2. comet  jquery
   3. comet  dojo

but I am not succeed with any of these attempts.

Discrimination : My query may not be relevant to Linux, but the tools[1]
were open source. People whoever feel its not relevant to them please do
ignore this thread.

[1] JavaScript frameworks
-- 
Ravi Jaya

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Tue Jun  9 22:39:35 2009
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Tue Jun  9 22:40:15 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] Tragedy: Successful Linux developer commits suicide
Message-ID: <a8f990120906091009p60733798r7f49bddf938bbbd0@mail.gmail.com>

Folks,

A tragic event today, following the (unrelated)
demise of Prof. Rajeev Motwani last week. A
successful Linux developer committed suicide in
Bangalore today - K.T.Ligesh, founder of LxLabs,
a Linux virtual server company apparently killed
himself after a security vulnerability was found in
his flagship app (the two events may be unrelated).
There were apparently no financial difficulties -
police say that his bank account had "crores".

http://www.channelregister.co.uk/2009/06/09/lxlabs_funder_death/

The Lxlabs home page as well as the product lineup
look very impressive, even by international standards.

http://lxlabs.com/

The hypervisor manager (?) that they offer looks very
polished, at least from the specs. Impressive work,
coming from a 32-year old. Tragic event, indeed -
hits closer home than the events surrounding
Hans Reiser a few years ago.

-Siva

I am facing some performance issues in squid .

i.e. I have Debian etch with squid,squidguard,shorewall.
Internet is? working in normal speed if clients are approx 50 .
If clients are approx 70 -100 it is getting very slow.

I googled for tuning and done the following things,
redirect_children 10
cache_dir ufs /var/spool/squid 1000 16 256
cache_mem 48 MB
pipeline_prefetch on
fqdncache_size 2048
maximum_object_size 8192 KB

Can you please suggest me how can i improve? much ?

FYI : We have Leased line .so we are getting constant bandwidth.
We are running the server in desktop HP Compaq with 4GB RAM, Core2Duo

On Wed, Jun 10, 2009 at 4:17 PM, Kenneth
Gonsalves<lawgon@thenilgiris.com> wrote:
>> Redmine :p
>> http://dev.tce.edu
>
> I don't understand - what is Redmine and where is it?

Redmine (http://www.redmine.org/) is a good alternative for trac.
Redmine comes with a major advantage that creating a project is so
simple and can be handled entirely over the web interface, unlike trac
in which you need to create new trac instance for each project. Also
if you are already using trac you can migrate all the components of
trac into a redmine site with ease. You can have a look at a working
redmine site here - http://dev.tce.edu/

-- 
Senthil Kumaran S
http://www.stylesen.org/

Date: Wed Jun 10 17:42:07 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] syslog-ng server - regarding
In-Reply-To: <64f5dd7b0906100440j14df6f32mda4c0697682f5e1@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0906101723280.1192-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

On 5:10pm, veera dv wrote:

> I was able to log message from client to my centralized server. my
> doubt is instead of using logger to check systlog_ng i want use
> command modprobe 3c509(i dont know how to use modprobe in syslog)

1. modprobe is used to load kernel module

2. If that kernel module, print(k) any message, klogd receives it 
   and send it to syslogd

3. The syslogd intern save it local file and pass it remote machine.

4. Suppose, if you want send the output message of modprobe command, 
   then, modprobe foo 2>&1 | logger

Bye :)
-- 
Bharathi S

On Wed, Jun 10, 2009 at 5:39 PM, mettur salem<metturmohan2009@gmail.com> wrote:
> Initially I dont have a *.svn* directory in the SVN repositary i created
> Recently,
> in server I am not able to create a ?Trunk and tag and branches ? please

If i understand it right, you are trying to create a directory in the
repository without a working copy. You can create something like:
  svn mkdir http://hostname.com/svn/proj/trunk -m "create trunk directory"
  svn mkdir http://hostname.com/svn/proj/branches -m "create tags directory"
  svn mkdir http://hostname.com/svn/proj/tags -m "create tags directory"

> Because of the last login user in svn repositary via http authentication (
> in Linux Server ) still cache its user name and password ?i try to create ?a
> trunk and branches and tag

You can pass --username option for any svn command to explicitly
specify a user to perform SVN operation. As per clearing or not using
cache, please take a look at --no-auth-cache option.

The good thing about Subversion, it is user friendly. You could have
got these queries clarified by simply viewing help for each sub
command. For instance,
  svn mkdir --help

would list all options you can pass with mkdir command. The 'svn help'
command would list all sub commands for Subversion. I know many others
have already pointed you to go through the manual. It does not look
like you did it so far. I request you to do it, believe it will
definitely save lot of your time.

Thank you.
-- 
Regards,
Bhuvaneswaran A

Hello,

On Wed, 10 Jun 2009, Balaviswa nathanv wrote:
> I need a one with GUI controls too

The web has a GUI interface and so does mail so that may not be the
point.

IMHO one difference is where the data is kept. With trac/redmine, the
discussion is on the web site. So if you want a local copy you need
to run something like wwwoffle and you need to subscribe to an RSS
feed to know when something has been commented on. Mail subscription
is sometimes possible but I am not sure how well these systems would
scale if 100's of people e-mail subscribed to various pages.

In the case of bugzilla, the discussion is archived centrally but
each subscriber gets a copy through mail _without_ additional
configuration. This copy can be kept for local reference by saving to
a folder.

In an increasingly networked world it is easy to forget where your
data actually is (and who controls it. ;-) ).

On the other hand creating discussion summaries over mail is really
much harder than doing it in a wiki like in trac. Reading through a
thread to figure out what the conclusion(s) was/were is terrible.

Kapil.
--

Hi,

--- On Wed, Jun 10, 2009 at 7:36 PM, Srinivas
G.<srinivasg@esntechnologies.co.in> wrote:
| 6) ? ? ?I have copied all the modules into the following path.
| ? ? ? ?/lib/modules/2.6.28/kernel/drivers/scsi
\--

Why? You can just insmod them directly.

---
| 7) ? ? ?Then reboot the system
\--

Err! Why are you rebooting? The point of making them as modules is
that you can load (insmod or modprobe) or unload (rmmod) them at
run-time without having to reboot.

---
| 8) ? ? ?Then, I have inserted a thumb drive. Then I am NOT able to see
| the debug statements that I added in the scsi.c and hosts.c files.
\--

But, did you check if the modules were loaded? Can you post lsmod output?

Also remember that SCSI Primary Commands-2 (SPC-2) specification, and
SCSI Block Commands ? 2 (SBC-2) commands are used by USB, and Linux
USB subsystem follows *SCSI emulation* for communication with mass
storage devices.

---
| Note: I have done almost the same procedure for the usb/storage drivers
| and I was able to see the debug messages there.
\--

Because usb_storage module is used:
http://lxr.linux.no/linux+v2.6.28/drivers/usb/storage/Kconfig#L9

---
| and I was not able to load scsi_mod as a module.
\--

You should have mentioned how you loaded the module, and what
output/error message you got. As mentioned earlier, check and post
lsmod output.

---
| When I opened
| menuconfig and checked for SCSI Device Support, I was not able to change
| it to module. The sign was "-*-". What does this sign signify.
\--

The module that it "depends" on hasn't been enabled (BLOCK) in the
configuration, perhaps?

Hi

Fedora 11, the latest and greatest version is now available. New
features include,

* Ext4 as the default filesystem for better performance and scalability

* yum-presto plugin for downloading binary deltas reducing download
sizes by over 80% typically

* Smoother and flicker free graphical boot using Plymouth and kernel
mode setting

* Firefox 3.5 and Thunderbird 3.0 pre-releases

* 20 second startup time

* Openchange for interoperability with Microsoft Exchange servers

* Desktop integration of multimedia codecs, fonts and more with
PackageKit, the graphical package manager in Fedora

* Nouveau as default Nvidia driver

* Better Fingerprint and Bluetooth support

* Several virtualization improvements including the latest KVM

* GNOME 2.26, KDE 4.2.3,  Xfce 4.6, Linux Kernel 2.6.29

.. and more

Get it at http://get.fedoraproject.org

More details at

http://fedoraproject.org/wiki/Fedora_11_tour

> I would like to know the difference between git and subversion?

git, like mercurial is a distributed version control system whereas subversion 
is a centralised one. As such, the former would seem more amenable to the 
bazaar style of development.

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Thu Jun 11 14:09:25 2009
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Thu Jun 11 14:10:01 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] Fedora 11 (Leonidas) Reigns
In-Reply-To: <4A30A4F2.4060200@fedoraproject.org>
References: <4A30A4F2.4060200@fedoraproject.org>
Message-ID: <a8f990120906110139y7fc96edeg3848452cfea18d17@mail.gmail.com>

On Thu, Jun 11, 2009 at 12:02 PM, Rahul Sundaram <sundaram@fedoraproject.org
> wrote:

> Hi
>
> Fedora 11, the latest and greatest version is now available. New
> features include,
>
> * Ext4 as the default filesystem for better performance and scalability
>
> * yum-presto plugin for downloading binary deltas reducing download
> sizes by over 80% typically
>
> * 20 second startup time
>
>
Yup, I checked it out an an Athlon-64/3200+ (2 GHz, single
core) with 1 GB dual-channel DDR 333 RAM and a 250 GB
SATA disk. Everything  was detected and  installed cleanly,
and with a few tricks I was able to get the boot times down
to 10-12 seconds to a text console.

1) Set runlevel to 3 in /etc/inittab
2) Turn off unnecessary services - YMMV, but for me
    that included Avahi, Bluetooth, rpc*, nfs*, and a few
    others. NetworkManager is another candidate.
3) Use a static IP instead of DHCP.
4) Disable  SELinux or set it to Permissive.

sub-5 second boots are within reach, but it may require a
dual- or quad-core box with the / partition mounted on a
striped (RAID 0) dual-SATA drive configuration, and /boot
on an SSD if possible.

-Siva

On Wed, Jun 10, 2009 at 8:00 PM, Kapil Hari Paranjape<kapil@imsc.res.in> wrote:
> Hello,
>
> On Wed, 10 Jun 2009, Balaviswa nathanv wrote:
>> I need a one with GUI controls too
>
> The web has a GUI interface and so does mail so that may not be the
> point.
>
> IMHO one difference is where the data is kept. With trac/redmine, the
> discussion is on the web site. So if you want a local copy you need
> to run something like wwwoffle and you need to subscribe to an RSS
> feed to know when something has been commented on. Mail subscription
> is sometimes possible but I am not sure how well these systems would
> scale if 100's of people e-mail subscribed to various pages.
>
> In the case of bugzilla, the discussion is archived centrally but
> each subscriber gets a copy through mail _without_ additional
> configuration. This copy can be kept for local reference by saving to
> a folder.
>
> In an increasingly networked world it is easy to forget where your
> data actually is (and who controls it. ;-) ).
>
> On the other hand creating discussion summaries over mail is really
> much harder than doing it in a wiki like in trac. Reading through a
> thread to figure out what the conclusion(s) was/were is terrible.
>
> Kapil.
> --
>
> _______________________________________________
> To unsubscribe, email ilugc-request@ae.iitm.ac.in with
> "unsubscribe <password> <address>"
> in the subject or body of the message.
> http://www.ae.iitm.ac.in/mailman/listinfo/ilugc
>

Hi,

--- On Thu, Jun 11, 2009 at 6:31 PM, Arulalan T<tarulalan@gmail.com> wrote:
| This example also covers of how to use active records in ruby.
|
| more at http://comboboxentry-glade-ruby.blogspot.com/
\--

#01 Did you create a blogspot just for this post?

#02 "Using this Chained Selection program , we are developing a school
management application with following scenerio ."

If you want to do a full-fledged application, use Rails making it
web-based. If you use Rails, controller, view, and model will be
separated neatly, as opposed to your current code.

#03 What editor are you using? Please check your code indentation.

#04 " :username => "root",
         :password =>"password",

Never check-in code with login details. Use Capistrano [1] for
deployment and you can provide the details there.

#05 create database ? country? in your mysql by excuting this query
      ?mysql > create database country; ?

All this should be automated using rake tasks. Don't ask the
administrator or other developers to do these manually.

#06 Also inculcate the practice of writing Ruby test cases as you develop code.

SK

[1] Capistrano. http://www.capify.org/

-- 
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

ILUGC Monthly Meet (Jun 13th):-
==============================

Time : Sat Jun 13th 15:00 IST 2009
Venue: ADI-TeNeT Seminar Hall,
       Room No: CSD 320,
       Electrical Science Block (ESB),
       IIT-Madras.

> Talk 1: Emacs-Org-Mode
Speaker : Ashok Gautham
Duration: ~40mins

Org-Mode is an emacs major mode that can be used for keeping notes,
maintaining ToDo lists, doing project planning, and authoring with
a fast and effective plain-text system. It comes in with a powerful
set of functions for maintaining spreadsheets and agendas.

Link: http://orgmode.org/

> Talk 2: Linux Config Files Series I - CUPS
Speaker : Raman P
Duration: ~40mins

This series of talk will cover most of the standard configuration
files in Linux based system. In this talk, Speaker will cover the
configuration files of the Common UNIX Printing System (CUPS),
a standards-based open source printing system.

Link: http://www.cups.org/

HTH :)

Bharathi S

On Fri, Jun 12, 2009 at 5:41 PM, Sudhir Gandotra
<sudhir.openlx@gmail.com> wrote:
> A manual, tough way, but the data is there, getting restored.
> One of them is here with me guessing the file names (or giving a near
> good name).
> I wish there was an automated way of doing it.
> Thanks a lot.

Prevention is better than cure.  Far better!

With so many online backup companies offering free/cheap
storage, there's really no reason not to backup your files remotely
and entirely avoid such peril.

To protect privacy, many backup systems can encrypt your data
even before it leaves your computer.

I use mozy on Windows and Areca (areca.sf.net) on linux. Mozy
gives me +2GB of free space, and my web hosting provider gives
me 50GB online space exclusively for off-site up data backup.

- Raja
From kapil at imsc.res.in  Fri Jun 12 19:52:15 2009
From: kapil at imsc.res.in (Kapil Hari Paranjape)
Date: Fri Jun 12 19:52:51 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] harddisk in trouble after fsck
In-Reply-To: <b1ab11c60906112341h4f4ed298i8892dca3845f6a05@mail.gmail.com>
References: <b1ab11c60906112341h4f4ed298i8892dca3845f6a05@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20090612142215.GA21042@imsc.res.in>

Hello,

On Fri, 12 Jun 2009, Sudhir Gandotra wrote:
> A harddisk on the laptop asked for fsck which was done.

It seems as if the wrong fsck was run or the system was erroneously
configured.

> Now, all the folders and files are gone and they seem to be in the
> lost+found directory and all the folders and files names have bene
> changed to numerical.

> How to recover the folders and files from the lost+found directory ?

These are _all_ the files which are recoverable but the process of
recovery will be painful because you need to identify each file.

> The help will be great for an NGO whose important data is in the disk.

Restore from your last good backup. (You did take a backup did you
not?)

Then look at each file in the lost+found directory to identify
those that are useful to you. Here are some tricks to speed up that
process:

 a. Ask your users to try to remember any important work that they
 did _after_ your last backup. This will allow you to narrow down the
 files you are looking for.

 b. Use the "file" command to figure out which files have which type.
 Then categoriese the files according to type.

 c. Use the "grep" command to search for particular strings in the
 document files which will help you categorise further.

 d. After that you will have no option but to actually view the files
 using a suitable viewer and see if that particular file is worth
 saving.

Regards,

Kapil.

P.S. Perhaps someone here knows how to use "beagle" or "xapian" to
simplify (b) and (c).

P.P.S. "The first time you lose data is usually the last time
that you forget to take a backup."
--

From linuxdassa at gmail.com  Wed Jun 17 14:24:15 2009
From: linuxdassa at gmail.com (Anu-Linux)
Date: Wed Jun 17 14:24:49 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] grep zip files without unzipping
In-Reply-To: <b423b9550906170138o64e1c856jc0dcf9da23143fea@mail.gmail.com>
References: <b423b9550906170138o64e1c856jc0dcf9da23143fea@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <9020ade10906170154wa6b64b7saca35f4a6c59b087@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

Did you try unzip command?

$ unzip -l zipfile.zip

will show you the contents of the archive without extracting it.

$ unzip -l zipfile.zip | grep JPG

will show you all the JPG files inside that archive.

HTH.

Cheers!

On Wed, Jun 17, 2009 at 2:24 PM, Anu-Linux <linuxdassa@gmail.com> wrote:

> Hi,
>
> Did you try unzip command?
>
> $ unzip -l zipfile.zip
>
> will show you the contents of the archive without extracting it.
>
> $ unzip -l zipfile.zip | grep JPG
>
> will show you all the JPG files inside that archive.


Thanks for your reply,I did it for recursive grep based on your suggestion
as shown below,

for file in *.zip ;
do
    unzip -l $file | grep -ir  jpg
    if [ $? = 0 ]
     then
      echo $file
   fi
done

The installer storage layer was completely rewritten from scratch and it
appears we are having some issues with it.

Do you get a traceback? If so can you post it or file it in bugzilla?
One thing to try is to use the default partition layout or try booting
with "textinst" to get the text installer.

In-Reply-To: <e43212340906172356t622976bcl864c58c419ad338e@mail.gmail.com>

>2009/6/18 ????????? <indianathann@gmail.com>

>
>
> /etc/wvdial.conf is as below
>
> [Dialer Defaults]
> Init2 = ATQ0 V1 E1 S0=0 &C1 &D2 +FCLASS=0
> [..]
> Username = <>
> Init1 = ATZ
> Password = <>
> Modem = /dev/ttyACM0
> Baud = 460800
> [..]
>
>
Try adding username (yourphone number) and password( may be your name) , try
running 'wvdialconf' is it detecting your modem? If wvdialconf command is
not detecting your modem, try changing the "baud" manually (tip if the
connection speed is 230kbps then change it to 203400) , i  got problem
connecting  bsnl wll phone internet , but changed the baud in
/etc/wvdial.conf manually  and  now  its working :)

Good luck.

windows.

From indianathann at gmail.com  Thu Jun 18 17:35:21 2009
From: indianathann at gmail.com (=?UTF-8?B?4K6q4K6k4K+N4K6u4K6o4K6+4K6k4K6p4K+N?=)
Date: Thu Jun 18 17:36:00 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] RE: Aircel mobile internet in Ubuntu 8.10 working
Message-ID: <e43212340906180505j5b56f44eo1bc2de6990c6ddca@mail.gmail.com>

LUGs,
           Aircel connection is working now.
/etc/wvdial.conf

[Dialer Defaults]
Init1 = ATZ
Init2 = ATQ0 V1 E1 S0=0 &C1 &D2 +FCLASS=0
Modem Type = USB Modem
Baud = 460800
New PPPD = 1
Modem = /dev/ttyACM0
ISDN = 0
Stupid Mode = 1
Phone =*99#
Username = a
Password = a
Init3 = AT+CGDCONT=1,"IP","aircelgprs.pr"
Dial Command = ATDT
Ask Password = 0
Compuserve =0
Auto DNS = 1
Flow Control = Hardware

                               Just googled and add some lines.

Thanks to all

Padhu,
Pollachi.

the correct baud rate.

We are receiving mails which reveal many people are confused regarding the article length.

Let me hence clearly state that the articles may be of 1 or 2 pages only. This is done so that each of the submitted articles may act as an inspiration or guide to the people, especially students without too many details.

Further the dates of the magazine are extended for all submissions till 22nd June, 2009 as per our previous mail. Articles may be submitted directly at the submission site. It does not require any approval by the magazine committee.

It is Dspace instituitional respository server. Each and every
administrative jobs like data entries are being done over web browser. But,
the problem here is, when our office networking becomes too much busy, our
data entry operator cannot input data there in my dspace server, it becomes
really really slow to submit any documents there in that Dspace server.

Now, i need to bypass our proxy server in order to boost up this data entry
operation. How can i do that? I mean, how can i make my Dspace server enable
for "bypassing proxy server"?

From sd.thinks at gmail.com  Fri Jun 19 16:00:25 2009
From: sd.thinks at gmail.com (S D)
Date: Fri Jun 19 16:01:23 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: ilugc Digest, Vol 61, Issue 35
In-Reply-To: <20090619063005.0B64C1DB25C@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
References: <20090619063005.0B64C1DB25C@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <55bf6c6f0906190330x5892cb64jefc03ed8c2d445f9@mail.gmail.com>

Aircel GPRS::

dnt have a complicated wvdial setting:

the dial no must be *99# and boud rate is 115200

the configuration shoull be

[Dialer Defaults]
Init1 = ATZ
Init2 = ATQ0 V1 E1 S0=0 &C1 &D2 +FCLASS=0
stupid mode = 1
Modem Type = Bluetooth Modem
Baud = 115200
New PPPD = yes
Modem = /dev/rfcomm0
ISDN = 0
Phone = *99#
Username = [Any No Or Text]
Password = [Any No Or Text]

save this configuration and restart your bluetooth!!
if still the problem persists then scan your phone for channel
details!! for more details read my blog
www.linuxlingo.wordpress.com hope you will resolve your problem :-)

On Fri, 2009-06-19 at 17:08 +0530, narendra babu wrote:

> I have few Linux/AIX/Windows servers  , I need to know how to identify
> how many NAS/SAN  storage are connected .
> 

Can you refine your query here? 

> I need to identify mount points for NAS/SAN , how i can differentaite
> from local mounts .

Do you have dedicated Storage on your network? 

With NAS, Samba, NFS, FTP shares are created and shared over the
network.

If NAS is configured properly, Places ---> Network in any modern GNU/
Linux GNOME desktop should help in locating it.

With regard to SAN, for redhat derivative you need to install
iscsi-initiator-utils package, and need to discover the target using
iscsiadm command.

for debian derivates, its open-iscsi pacakge.

these links should help,

http://www.cyberciti.biz/faq/howto-setup-debian-ubuntu-linux-iscsi-initiator/
http://www.cyberciti.biz/tips/rhel-centos-fedora-linux-iscsi-howto.html

From lgp171188 at gmail.com  Sat Jun 20 17:19:26 2009
From: lgp171188 at gmail.com (Guruprasad)

Subject: [Ilugc] Changing the screen resolution on Debian Lenny
Message-ID: <7c956f0c0906200449s253b4341n501b1e4f59f5eaa3@mail.gmail.com>

Hi all,
I have been a Debian user since Debian Etch and have moved on to Lenny
with its release. There is an issue which I faced in a few computers
with screen resolution. The computers which were running with 1024x768
as the default maximum resolution supported a maximum resolution of
800x600 when upgraded to Lenny.

Normally to sort out issues with screen resolution, I use
'dpkg-reconfigure xserver-xorg' wherein I will be able to configure
the screen resolution. But in lenny, there seems to be o provision to
do the same. How can get this job done without manually having to edit
the configuration files?

Thank you.

Regards,
Guruprasad.
From kapil at imsc.res.in  Sat Jun 20 18:38:43 2009
From: kapil at imsc.res.in (Kapil Hari Paranjape)
Date: Sat Jun 20 18:39:22 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] Changing the screen resolution on Debian Lenny
In-Reply-To: <7c956f0c0906200449s253b4341n501b1e4f59f5eaa3@mail.gmail.com>
References: <7c956f0c0906200449s253b4341n501b1e4f59f5eaa3@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20090620130843.GA4547@imsc.res.in>

Hello,

On Sat, 20 Jun 2009, Guruprasad wrote:
> Normally to sort out issues with screen resolution, I use
> 'dpkg-reconfigure xserver-xorg' wherein I will be able to configure
> the screen resolution.

You can also try 
  dpkg-reconfigure -plow xserver-xorg
This will allow to access to a few more configuration variables.

Note that more recent (squeeze?) xserver-xorg setups use _no_
configuration file by default (which is not without controversy as you
can imagine!). This is because the xserver queries the hardware and
sets up things automatically.

So if you have a specific configuration file that you like then you
should make a copy of it and use it. Note also that Debian generally
keeps a backup of your configuration files in
 /etc/X11/xorg.conf.<date>
If an older configuration file worked better for you then you can use
that. Of course, this only applies is you upgrade --- motto is
"upgrade, do re-install".

Regards,

Kapil.
--

On Sat, Jun 20, 2009 at 6:46 PM, Guruprasad<lgp171188@gmail.com> wrote:
> Even with 'dpkg-reconfigure -plow xserver-xorg' there is no provision
> to tweak the resolution configuration.

Try moving the /etc/X11/xorg.conf file. Newer Xorg auto detects and
configures the required values. I am not sure what version of Xorg
does lenny have. I had this problem when I upgraded ubuntu 8.04 to
8.10. Removing the xorg.conf did the trick.

Hello,

On Sat, 20 Jun 2009, Guruprasad wrote:
> IIRC, the same 'dpkg-reconfigure xserver-xorg' used to allow the
> screen resolution to be configured.  But it appears to be no longer
> the same on lenny.

You are correct. The debconf templates do not have values for the
resolution.

> But the screen resolution is automagically configured to a
> resolution lesser than the maximum resolution supported.

How do you know that a larger resolution is supported? Perhaps the
combination worked in the past but is unstable with the new xserver
and could crash and/or damage the equipment. :-|

> Are there any ways to overcome this?

Yes. Create your own /etc/X11/xorg.conf file and install it. All the
tweaking of the configuration that was possible in the past is still
possible. :-)

This file can be created in many ways. As mentioned earlier, there is
also a backup copy of this file when systems are upgraded.

Best of luck,

Kapil.
--

	<7c956f0c0906200758u5a756048p61a322a433552231@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20090620224724.GA19536@imsc.res.in>

Hello,

On Sat, 20 Jun 2009, Guruprasad wrote:
> A resolution of 1024x768 was available on Debian Etch installation on
> the same machine.

Have a look at /var/log/Xorg.0.log you may get some hints as to why a
higher resolution is being rejected by the automatic process.

One reason that occasionally shows up is "shared memory" video cards.
For such a card, adjusting the available memory in BIOS can sometimes
do the trick.

Regards,

Kapil.
--

From kapil at imsc.res.in  Sun Jun 21 23:21:01 2009
From: kapil at imsc.res.in (Kapil Hari Paranjape)
Date: Sun Jun 21 23:21:34 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] FLASH equivalent for Linux
In-Reply-To: <28ac23fb0906210917k1482711am649a21a63790c07f@mail.gmail.com>
References: <28ac23fb0906210917k1482711am649a21a63790c07f@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20090621175101.GA3645@imsc.res.in>

Hello,

On Sun, 21 Jun 2009, bala chandar wrote:
>  I need an alternative to create FLASH animations in ubuntu.I tried
> Flash with wine.But I need an exact open source alternative.Is there
> any solution for it. I didnt find any good solutions in google too.

Google is not a search-all. (Neither is bing for that matter).

Here is how you would start answering such a question yourself:
 apt-cache search flash

This will, of course, show up a number of applications that are not
relevant (debtags is better). But by looking through the list you find
can truncate it to something like this:

 kipi-plugins, bleachbit, flasm, flvtool2, freej, haxe, libming-util,
 mtasc, ploticus, pyvnc2swf, salasaga, swfmill, swftools, yamdi, warsow

You can then run:
 apt-cache show {pkgname}
for each of these pkgname's and figure out that some useful ones are:

 kipi, flasm, flvtool2, haxe, libming-util, mtasc, ploticus,
 salasaga, swfmill, yamdi

You can further trim these based on your needs or decide that none of
these do what you want ( :-( ).

_Then_ you can post to the help lists like ilugc asking for more
information not neglecting to mention the results of your prior
research.

The above is meant as "constructive criticism" which you can follow
in future. :-)

Regards,

Kapil.
--

Message: 4
Date: Sun, 21 Jun 2009 23:21:01 +0530
From: Kapil Hari Paranjape <kapil@imsc.res.in>
Subject: Re: [Ilugc] FLASH equivalent for Linux
To: ILUG-C <ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <20090621175101.GA3645@imsc.res.in>
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii

Hello,

On Sun, 21 Jun 2009, bala chandar wrote:
>? I need an alternative to create FLASH animations in ubuntu.I tried
> Flash with wine.But I need an exact open source alternative.Is there
> any solution for it. I didnt find any good solutions in google too.

Google is not a search-all. (Neither is bing for that matter).

Here is how you would start answering such a question yourself:
apt-cache search flash

This will, of course, show up a number of applications that are not
relevant (debtags is better). But by looking through the list you find
can truncate it to something like this:

kipi-plugins, bleachbit, flasm, flvtool2, freej, haxe, libming-util,
mtasc, ploticus, pyvnc2swf, salasaga, swfmill, swftools, yamdi, warsow

You can then run:
apt-cache show {pkgname}
for each of these pkgname's and figure out that some useful ones are:

kipi, flasm, flvtool2, haxe, libming-util, mtasc, ploticus,
salasaga, swfmill, yamdi

You can further trim these based on your needs or decide that none of
these do what you want ( :-( ).

_Then_ you can post to the help lists like ilugc asking for more
information not neglecting to mention the results of your prior
research.

The above is meant as "constructive criticism" which you can follow
in future. :-)

Regards,

Kapil.
--

>  kipi-plugins, bleachbit, flasm, flvtool2, freej, haxe, libming-util,
>  mtasc, ploticus, pyvnc2swf, salasaga, swfmill, swftools, yamdi, warsow
>
> You can then run:
>  apt-cache show {pkgname}
> for each of these pkgname's and figure out that some useful ones are:
>
>  kipi, flasm, flvtool2, haxe, libming-util, mtasc, ploticus,
>  salasaga, swfmill, yamdi
>
> You can further trim these based on your needs or decide that none of
> these do what you want ( :-( ).
>
> _Then_ you can post to the help lists like ilugc asking for more
> information not neglecting to mention the results of your prior
> research.
>
> The above is meant as "constructive criticism" which you can follow
> in future. :-)
>
> Regards,
>
> Kapil.

           Hi,
               Thanks for the tip.I ll surely search with apt-cache
before post my next question.
                                 cheers..
From thescriptdevil at gmail.com  Mon Jun 22 21:18:35 2009
From: thescriptdevil at gmail.com (Ashok Gautham)
Date: Mon Jun 22 21:19:32 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] Request to Digest Mode Subscribers
Message-ID: <3232b7ed0906220848t474efd0bpf7ecf71dd73ca2e7@mail.gmail.com>

I am most certainly not the admin of this LUG, but I would like to
take interest in the welfare of this mailing list.

If you are ever planning to reply in the LUG, the digest mode is not
what you want. Asking questions is a different beast since you create
the new subject. I would suggest you do the following.

A) You want to be active on the LUG

i) Create a new email-id for the lug.  eg. If your name/nick of choice
is Foo Bar/FooBar, create a gmail id called FooBar.ilugc@gmail.com. (I
had a spare id that I created by mistake).

ii) Unsubscribe from the LUG mailing list for the old id
http://www.ae.iitm.ac.in/mailman/listinfo/ilugc

iii) Resubscribe with the new id through the same page. ( You do not
lose any karma points for doing so :P ). This time, you know that you
have subscribed for only the LUG (and possibly a few other mailing
lists). So use the normal mode. Do not choose the digest mode

B) If you are passive on the mailing list or want to only ask
questions,
i) I would still recommend A
ii) Snip the unnecessary parts of the digest mail and retain only the
parts that you need
iii) *CHANGE THE SUBJECT* from Digest Volume XYZ to the real subject
of the conversation

I would still recommend that you subscriibe to the normal mode of the
mailing list. If you use gmail, you can put multiple inboxes to good
use for this. Create a filter for lug messages, add a label to it in
the actions option of the filter and use a separate inbox frame for
that filter alone.

By subscribing to the digest and changing the title, you are still
possibly ruining the coherency and the context of the message as
gmail(which most use) and most other email clients may not be able to
classify them as a part of the same thread. This ruins the flow of the
thread.
I find that you may be able to retain it in the same thread by keeping the
title as

Re: [ilugc] <Original Title in the thread>.
Do not prefix another Re: Use the initial thread posts's title

Any more tips are welcome.
---
Ashok `ScriptDevil` Gautham
From kapil at imsc.res.in  Mon Jun 22 21:45:49 2009
From: kapil at imsc.res.in (Kapil Hari Paranjape)
Date: Mon Jun 22 21:46:27 2009

Hello,

Disclaimer: I do have a gmail account but I do not use it (a) much
or (b) via the web.

On Mon, 22 Jun 2009, Ashok Gautham wrote:
> i) Create a new email-id for the lug.  eg. If your name/nick of choice
> is Foo Bar/FooBar, create a gmail id called FooBar.ilugc@gmail.com. (I
> had a spare id that I created by mistake).

I am curious as to why you suggest this.

Does gmail does not have a way to automatically classify incoming mail
into different mail folders? I recall something called "tags" which
seemed to be similar to mail folders.

The digest mode is for people who wish to see the messages only
once in a while _and_ use an antiquated mail program.

With most modern mail programs it is easy to classifying incoming mail
into folders so that one does not have to read a particular folder
until one wants to. You can even set up "auto-aging" so that messages
older than a certain date are automatically erased.

There are a number of reasons why one should try to use one (or a
small number of) e-mail id(s) for as long as possible. Primarily, in
the FOSS world it allows people to identify your interaction with the
community.

Regards,

Kapil.

On Mon, 2009-06-22 at 21:45 +0530, Kapil Hari Paranjape wrote:
> Does gmail does not have a way to automatically classify incoming mail
> into different mail folders? I recall something called "tags" which
> seemed to be similar to mail folders.

Gmail does have filters, and as an alternative to using a different
email address, you can modify the address you give out. For instance,
mail sent to ilovepigs+cows@gmail.com, ilovepigs@gmail.com, and
i.love.pigs@gmail.com will all reach the same person's inbox. If you so
wish, you can then filter the mail based on which address it was sent
to. Pretty cool, eh?

Roshan George <roshan@arjie.com>

p.sriram wrote:
> well, there is a web front end through the news gateway at gmane. this can be 
> used to reply to list postings (like i am doing right now). the gmane web 
> front end is at 
> 
>  http://news.gmane.org/thread.php?group=gmane.org.user-groups.linux.ilugc

gmane also provides 'nntp' access, you can configure your mail
client(I'm using thunderbird) to read posts. Here is what I did.

1. Subscribed to ilugc,

2. loggedin to ilugc account page and disabled mail delivery option.

3. In thunderbird, I opened file->new->account->newgroup account wizard.

4. In subsequent clicks, it will ask for newgroup server, I filled
news.gmane.org and gave account name as 'Gmane'.

5. I got 'Gmane' in the left side panel. right clicked 'Gmane' and in
the context menu, I selected 'subscribe'

6. A little search for 'ilugc' and found the 'gmane' address of ilugc.
Also attached it to sidepanel.

7. Now I'm reading 'ilugc' post through thunderbird (using 'gmane'
servers). If we want to reply to a post, click reply and send the mail
to the 'gmane' address of ilugc. First time gmane will send an alert
mail saying that you must be subscribed to the original mailing list.
Reply yes to gmane. Your mail will appear within 3 to 5 min in the
mailing-list.

I think most of the modern mail clients have newsgroup reader. AFAIK,
'gmane.org' is the only site which is giving 'nntp' access to their
servers. I don't know much about 'nntp' but people used/using it to read
 usenet posts.

http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Network_News_Transfer_Protocol

HIH :)

Regards,
Mohan R

From sagarun at gmail.com  Tue Jun 23 12:12:08 2009
From: sagarun at gmail.com (Arun SAG)
Date: Tue Jun 23 12:13:06 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] [FWD] Invitation to meeting of the National network of the
	FOSS Community in India(FOSSCOMM)
In-Reply-To: <4A3F17FF.5040606@itforchange.net>
References: <4A3F17FF.5040606@itforchange.net>
Message-ID: <dee9e8140906222342pe96042ej68a22420dee3118e@mail.gmail.com>

FYI ,Forwarded message....

Dear All,

Many of us have been advocating for several years, the adoption of FOSS
applications and platforms in our country. FOSS related advocacy has
been gradually gathering energies, including the campaign against
software patents, including FOSS in the CBSE syllabi , suggesting a FOSS
manifesto for political parties in the recent elections etc.

However, we do have a long way to go before FOSS is taken as a default
software option. Towards this cause, a network or a coalition of
organizations working on FOSS adoption and promotion, would be able to
act more cohesively on issues and strengthen our individual efforts.
While such an initiative will be energy-intensive and time-consuming, it
would help orchestrate our advocacy for FOSS adoption. We are writing to
you to invite you to a meeting to discuss the building of such a
coalition comprising of members from academic institutions, NGOs and
CBOs, research and advocacy groups, professional associations, FOSS
enterprises, FOSS user groups, government officials, media professionals
etc and also its possible priorities.

The first meeting of this network was held in Bangalore in February 09,
when over 30 people met and discussed issues including working with
Universities in Karnataka through NRC-FOSS, to adopt FOSS, train
teachers on GNU/Linux (the Karnataka Computer learning program in
schools is on GNU/Linux), countering monopolistic and restrictive
practices in the IT sector, technical aspects such as developing local
language fonts that are Unicode compliant etc. A mailing list and a wiki
(http://fosscomm.in) have been since created.Please see the
wiki(http://fosscomm.in) for a more detailed update on that meeting and
activities post that meeting.

We now plan to continue building this coalition, with a meeting in
Delhi. We request you to join for a full-day meeting on the 4th of July
at the JNU, New Delhi (exact venue within JNU will be communicated shortly).

The proposed (draft) agenda for the meeting is as follows-
1. Reporting on the Bangalore FOSSCOMM 1st Meeting and follow up

2. ?Open Standards? Follow up on the Department of IT's draft policy on
open standards (http://www.mit.gov.in/download/Policyonopensandards.pdf)
3. FOSS in Education
What the FOSS community can do to promote the use of FOSS in School
Education and Higher Education

4. Software Patents and other legal issues
a) Take up pre and post grant opposition for selected cases
b) Take up the issue of Draft Manual which deviates from the Patent Act
c) Take up with the Competition Commission, practices which seem to be
restrictive or monopolistic.

5. Building political consensus around FOSS as an important factor for
India's development

If you require accommodation, please let us know, we will try and
arrange at JNU.
The travel costs as well as the cost of stay would have to be borne by
the participants.

For those requesting accommodation, please write to the following:
Prof. Andrew Lynn lynn.andrew@gmail.com <lynn.andrew%40gmail.com> and Rajesh
Kalithody -
myidrajesh@gmail.com <myidrajesh%40gmail.com>

Any suggestion/modifications to the agenda are welcome.

Thanks,

socio-economic development of some of the most marginalized and

accessible credit for small enterprise to the rural poor. For

track community members' savings and loans. We are looking for
developers who can provide a web-based solution towards this end.

From rajasuperman at gmail.com  Tue Jun 23 14:05:07 2009
From: rajasuperman at gmail.com (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Tue Jun 23 14:06:03 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] BlackBerry - GPRS without BIS
In-Reply-To: <3b0107320906230054k271f1c58m769797dbd66c787c@mail.gmail.com>
References: <a3b05e8b0906220515v364dec52gaddb5099a3b0f5df@mail.gmail.com> 
	<92f9a9560906230008n36130113rd861f81668591217@mail.gmail.com> 
	<3b0107320906230054k271f1c58m769797dbd66c787c@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <92f9a9560906230135u4b4d5aa0tbecc593d1272fae2@mail.gmail.com>

On Tue, Jun 23, 2009 at 1:24 PM, CreativeWolf<creativewolf@gmail.com> wrote:
> BIS is for pushing mail and alike and GPRS is supposed to be independent
> using their APN & goes through a proxy thus restricted to a particular port
> mostly 80 and applications that use sockets wouldn't work thats when the
> Data Plan comes to rescue which uses EDGE.

BB explicitly requires BB data service to be enabled for your SIM card
by the service provider.  You cannot take the SIM card out of a Nokia
smart phone which has Airtel Mobile Office (GPRS) enabled, and use
it in a BB -- only voice calls will work, no data of any sort.

Nearly all telcos bundle BB data plan and BIS for their subscribers.


> Pretty nifty these service providers who make the best out of it all.

RIM has a hand in it too -- BB is not a regular GSM/CDMA phone, it
requires support from the service provider for many data/smart phone
functions.

Also, moving a BB which is SIM locked to one telco to another is very
difficult, or very expensive.

BB is a nice platform, but a very closed one.

- Raja

I think you've missed the {_____:script=taml} in the font tag that you've
used. Please check
The following seemed to work well for me.


\documentclass[a4paper]{article}
\usepackage{fontspec}
\font\tamilRoman="TAMu_Maduram:script=taml" at 12pt

\begin{document}

\title{\tamilRoman ???????????}
\author{\tamilRoman ????????????}
\date{}
\maketitle

\section{\tamilRoman ???????? 1 : ?????? ????????}
\tamilRoman
??? ???? ????????????? ??? \\
????? ??????? ???? \\

????????? ?? ?????????? ???????? \\
??????? ??????? ????? \\

\end{document}

By the way, you could've posted this in the tugindia mailing list as well. I
believe TeX/LaTeX related q's are better answered there.

From siva.chandran.p at gmail.com  Thu Jun 25 12:38:15 2009
From: siva.chandran.p at gmail.com (Siva Chandran P)
Date: Thu Jun 25 12:38:52 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] Catalog Builder - Create catalog for your movie collection
Message-ID: <e3a31dcd0906250008v7bef97aao55208b36287daaae@mail.gmail.com>

Catalog Builder is desktop application that generates catalog for your
movie collection. First it collects the movie files and strips any
unwanted characters/words from the filename. Then it tries guess the
movie title from the filename and fetches the movie information from
imdb.org. Finally it generates the catalog from the collected
information.

For more information visit
http://www.sivachandran.in/index.php/projects/catalog-builder

Siva Chandran P
From mbhangui at gmail.com  Thu Jun 25 14:49:16 2009
From: mbhangui at gmail.com (Manvendra Bhangui)
Date: Thu Jun 25 14:49:54 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] Linux Mail - indimail at sourceforge.net - GPLV3
Message-ID: <95c27c8c0906250219u32d27af9q4b8416aada871093@mail.gmail.com>

IndiMail is a enterprise class MailServer (http://www.indimail.org)
which can serve users in a virtual domain split across multiple
servers for horizontal scalability. IndiMail allows the same domain to
be located on geographical different locations without requiring a
distributed file system like NFS, etc.
IndiMail can be useful for SMEs who can use a robust mail server
without spending a single rupee on
unethical software licenses. IndiMail also can be used to tie a domain
across a heterogeneous set of mail servers (e.g. mix of exchange,
lotus notes, postfix, etc)

The architecture is highly scalable and one can keep on adding users
for a domain on different servers. The MTA is a highly modified
version of qmail. The mail queue on IndiMail is a collection of
multiple queues which gives IndiMail to handle massive amount of mail
traffic. A typical architecture
can be seen  here
https://sourceforge.net/project/screenshots.php?group_id=230686

IndiMail provides proxy for SMTP/SMTPS, POP3/POP3S, IMAP/IMAPS. The
proxies allows anyone to seamlessly migrate from a proprietary
solutions like Lotus Notes or MS Exchange. The same proxy allows any
user to access/send mails from any location regardless of which server
the user's mailbox lies. IndiMail also provides everything in one
package that a typical mail server requires (virus scanner, antispam,
imap, pop3, etc).

IndiMail was first released at Midnight Aug 15, 2008 to provide
freedom from proprietary solutions and is currently on Release 1.5. It
has been tested to handle around 3 Million+ accounts and > 4 million
deliveries / day. In my organization, IndiMail has beaten postfix in
speed at much lower server loads. You all are welcome to try this out.
A single server like the HP DL 380 has been tested to serve 100,000
users.

The full feature list can be read here
http://groups.google.com/group/indimail/web/detailed-feature

IndiMail supports all standard mail protocols. It is one of the few
mailservers which is DKIM ready. IndiMail's DKIM also supports ADSP
(Author Domain Signing Practice).
See http://www.dkim.org/deploy/IndiMail.html

IndiMail currently works only on reliable OS like Linux, Mac OS X. Any
attempt to compile IndiMail on Windows will stubbornly fail and
shouldn't be attempted (even at your own risk).

IndiMail can be configured through a set of Environment variables or
control files.
There are around 200 parameters which can be used to set any feature
of IndiMail.

A powerful concept called envrules allows you to set Indimail
differently for different users.
The source can be downloaded at
http://sourceforge.net/project/platformdownload.php?group_id=230686

IndiMail also has yum repositories for most of the Linux Distros at

http://download.opensuse.org/repositories/home:/mbhangui/

You will also find the RPMs for both 32bit and 64bit OS on the above repository

ReadyMade binaries are available in RPM form for the following distros

* SUSE
          o openSUSE 11.1
          o openSUSE 11.0
          o SUSE Linux Enterprise 10
          o openSUSE Factory

    * Red Hat
          o Fedora 10
          o Fedora 9
          o Red Hat Enterprise Linux 5
          o CentOS 5

    * Mandriva Linux
          o Mandriva 2009
          o Mandriva 2008

A installer for Mac OS X and a debian package for Ubuntu and Debian
are in the works. IndiMail requires volunteers for platforms apart
from those listed above. Everyone is welcome to contribute. Everyone
is welcome to rip apart the code and find bugs or give suggestions. I
will also welcome anyone who can provide me a free shell account on
Ubuntu/Debian so that I can build a debian package.

For me writing IndiMail has been a passion. IndiMail is not a
commercial project and never will be. However, I welcome anyone who
would want to provide commercial support for Installation,
configuration, setup and architecting.

There are four Mailing Lists for IndiMail

1. indimail-support - You can subscribe for Support at
   https://lists.sourceforge.net/lists/listinfo/indimail-support. You can email
   indimail-support@lists.sourceforge.net for posting messages to this
list. Old discussions
   can be seen here.

2. indimail-devel   - You can subscribe at
    https://lists.sourceforge.net/lists/listinfo/indimail-devel.
    You can email indimail-devel@lists.sourceforge.net for posting
messages to this list.
    Old discussions can be seen here.

3. Archive at Google - http://groups.google.com/group/indimail.
    This group acts as a remote archive for both indimail-support and
     indimail-devel list at sourceforge.
     Any discussions posted here goes to indimail-support.

4. indimail-announce - This is only meant for announcement of New
Releases or patches.
   You can subscribe at http://groups.google.com/group/indimail.

Indimail also has a blog at http://indimail.blogspot.com/
You can tweet IndiMail at http://twitter.com/indimail
IndiMail can also be seen on facebook at
http://www.facebook.com/home.php#/pages/indimail/88063516703

--
Regards Manvendra - http://www.indimail.org
