Date: Thu Jun 25 14:56:29 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] tamil unicode with xelatex
In-Reply-To: <1245777358.3620.15.camel@debian>
References: <1245777358.3620.15.camel@debian>
Message-ID: <1245922093.5418.12.camel@debian>

On Tue, 2009-06-23 at 22:45 +0530, Joshua Immanuel wrote:
> \font\lang="Lohit Tamil"\lang
> 
I found the solution for it. Though I mention the font name to use I
have to explicitly mention the behaviour of the font using the script
tag. When the above line was changed to

\font\lang="Lohit Tamil:script=taml"

the fonts got rendered properly and here is the screenshot.
http://www.flickr.com/photos/26427529@N05/3658929869/

The reference for the above solution was found at
http://xetex.wiki.sourceforge.net/commands-font

regards
-- 
Joshua Immanuel.

> movie collection. First it collects the movie files and strips any

From bhargavprasanna at gmail.com  Fri Jun 26 14:08:14 2009
From: bhargavprasanna at gmail.com (Bhargav Prasanna)
Date: Fri Jun 26 14:08:49 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] Pidgin connectivity with Yahoo
In-Reply-To: <5ef2113c0906260041m21658b64r1f7a1bc4fddcacd7@mail.gmail.com>
References: <5ef2113c0906260041m21658b64r1f7a1bc4fddcacd7@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <e6b5008a0906260138p70103f7bn7d7513c6cc44ad33@mail.gmail.com>

On 6/26/09, Senthil Kumaran S <stylesen@gmail.com> wrote:
> Hi,
>
> I ve been using pidgin for a long time now in my debian lenny box and
> some ubuntu boxes. I ve found out that for the past one week, I am
> unable to connect to Yahoo accounts using pidgin. Is there something
> changed? do someone else face the same problem. My pidgin version is
> 2.4.3 on debian lenny system with all latest updates installed.


Go to your yahoo account settings in Pidgin. You'll see two tabs at
the top. Go to the second tab. There you'll find, "scs.msg.yahoo.com"
and a few other web addresses.. Open a terminal, ping all the
addresses separately and replace the addresses with the numerical IP
address you see when you ping.
Restart Pidgin and try connecting again..

HTH.. =)

-- 
Cheers,

	<69621d830906260809oebf7e9dr2c02d781c99c835a@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20090626163821.GA5702@imsc.res.in>

Hello,

On Fri, 26 Jun 2009, Zico wrote:
> Actually, i want to find out, what that employee actually did, which created
> such situation.

Why don't you ask the employee? Or don't you trust your employees?
:-)

By the way logging in as root via the GUI on a shared system is not
such a great idea _unless_ you trust your users.

A clever user can easily use various ruses to get your password.

For example, it is relatively easy to run qemu in fullscreen mode and
get a prompt *exactly* like the one running on the base system. Now if
this qemu is running with key-logging, your root password would get
recorded.

There are many other such tricks.

It is safer to login over the network using ssh from a machine to
which only you have access. One other option is to use the SAK key
(usually Alt+SysRq+K) after switching to a text-mode console. This
will ensure that you are actually running the system "getty".

Regards,

Kapil.
--

From kapil at imsc.res.in  Tue Jun 30 19:13:10 2009
From: kapil at imsc.res.in (Kapil Hari Paranjape)
Date: Tue Jun 30 19:13:46 2009
Subject: [Ilugc] Problem with suspending in Fedora 10
In-Reply-To: <dee9e8140906300117n1791af5v1955ad15286ea85e@mail.gmail.com>
References: <d884cbab0906292158v7637b840h9e601e27e43b91f4@mail.gmail.com>
	<dee9e8140906300117n1791af5v1955ad15286ea85e@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20090630134310.GA16507@imsc.res.in>

Hello,

On Tue, 30 Jun 2009, Arun SAG wrote:
> For me most of the applications like system monitor and NetworkManager
> crashes after suspending and resuming my laptop(DELL inspiron 1525) in
> gnome.

If you _can_ resume, then the problem is to do with specific
hardware peripherals. 

In most cases, the problem is with video hardware, so if that is
working for you then you are almost done. If not, then be prepared to
spend a lot of time with problem --- start by suspending/resuming
with X.

Some wireless card drivers need to be unloaded before suspend and
re-loaded after resume. I don't know if network manager can handle
such a situation and may be crashing as a consequence.

This is one reason why getting a laptop which has a pre-installed
GNU/Linux with all features working is a good idea. It means that you
_know_ that it all "Just Works".

Doesn't Dell offer Ubuntu pre-installed on the Inspiron series?

Regards,

Kapil.
--
